    <a name="LUHMANN">
    </a>
   </p>
   <table cellpadding="4" width="100%">
    <tr>
     <td bgcolor="#336699">
      <a href="#top" target="_self">
       <img align="right" alt="Index" border="0" src="../images/up.gif"/>
      </a>
      <font color="WHITE" size="2">
       <b>
        Luhmann, Niklas
       </b>
       [1927 - 1998]
      </font>
     </td>
    </tr>
   </table>
   <p>
    <b>
     By Luhmann
    </b>
   </p>
   <ul>
    <img align="right" alt="Niklas Luhmann" src="../images/sociologists/luhmann.gif"/>
    <li>
     <a href="http://www.uni-bielefeld.de/sozsys/leseproben/luhmann.htm">
      Causality in the South
     </a>
     <br/>
     Niklas Luhmann,
     <i>
      Soziale Systeme,
     </i>
     1995:1.
     <br/>
     <span style="line-height:17px;font-size:11px;">
      Policies of development using legal and monetary mechanisms have not been very successful. Resistance against modernization has been explained by factors such as tradition, culture, mentalities. For Luhmann these are more or less tautological explanations. He proposes to replace them by the factor social construction of causality. Relations between causes and effects can no longer be treated as objective aspects of the world and as a question of true or false judgment. Rather, causality is an infinity of possible combinations of causes and effects which requires highly selective attribution processes to be of any cognitive or practical value. In Luhmanns mind  causality is a medium of loosely couples possibilities which requires the selection of forms, i.e. tight couplings, of interesting causes and interesting effects.
     </span>
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1995]
     <a href="http://www.soziale-systeme.ch/leseproben/luhmann.htm">
      Kausalitt im Sden
     </a>
     <br/>
     In: Soziale Systeme 1(1): 7-28.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [2000]
     <a href="http://www.uni-bielefeld.de/sozsys/pdf/luhmann1.pdf">
      Das Medium der Religion. Eine soziologische Betrachtung ber Gott und die Seelen
     </a>
     [pfd]
     <br/>
     In: Soziale Systeme 6(1): 39-53.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [2008]
     <a href="http://www.soziale-systeme.ch/pdf/sozsys_1-2008_luhmann-norms.pdf">
      Are There Still Indispensable Norms in Our Society?
     </a>
     <br/>
     In: Soziale Systeme 14(1): 18-37. Translation of Gibt es in unserer Gesellschaft noch onverzichtbare Normen? (1993).
    </li>
   </ul>

    <a name="MALINOWSKI">
    </a>
   </p>
   <table cellpadding="4" width="100%">
    <tr>
     <td bgcolor="#336699">
      <a href="#top" target="_self">
       <img align="right" alt="Index" border="0" src="../images/up.gif"/>
      </a>
      <font color="WHITE" size="2">
       <b>
        Malinowski, Bronislaw
       </b>
       [1884 - 1942]
      </font>
     </td>
    </tr>
   </table>
   <p>
    <b>
     <i>
      By Malinowski
     </i>
    </b>
   </p>
   <ul>
    <img align="right" alt="Bronislaw Malinowski" src="../images/sociologists/malinowski.jpg"/>
    <li>
     [1916]
     <a href="http://www.sacred-texts.com/pac/baloma/index.htm">
      Baloma; the Spirits of the Dead in the Trobriand Islands
     </a>
     <br/>
     In: The Journal of the Royal Anthropological Institute of Great Britain and Ireland, Volume 46.
     <br/>
     <span style="line-height:17px;font-size:11px;">
      The Trobriand Islanders of the Melanesian region, as well as many other cultures in the Australian and New Guinea regions, had a belief that there was no cause and effect relationship between sexual intercourse and pregnancy. The Trobrianders believed that the Baloma, the spirits of the dead, would return from the afterlife and impregnate women when they bathed in the lagoon, thus reincarnating the dead ancestor. A classical study of one of the founders of modern ethnography.
     </span>
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1921]
     <a href="http://classiques.uqac.ca/classiques/malinowsli/sexualite_repression/sexualite_repression.html">
      La sexualit et sa rpression dans les socits primitives
     </a>
     <br/>
     French translation of
     <i>
      The sexual Life of Savages in North-Western Melanesia
     </i>
     .
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1932]
     <a href="http://archive.org/details/argonautsofthewe032976mbp">
      Argonauts Of The Western Pacific
     </a>
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1933]
     <a href="http://classiques.uqac.ca/classiques/malinowsli/moeurs__et_coutumes_melanesiens/0_moeurs_et_coutumes/moeurs_et_coutumes.html">
      Moeurs et coutumes des Mlansiens
     </a>
     <br/>
     Trois essais sur la vie sociale des primitifs.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1941]
     <a href="http://classiques.uqac.ca/classiques/malinowsli/dynamiques_evolution/dynamiques_evolution.html">
      Les dynamiques de lvolution culturelle
     </a>
     <br/>
     Recherche sur les relations raciales en Afrique.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1944]
     <a href="http://classiques.uqac.ca/classiques/malinowsli/theorie_culture/theorie_culture.html">
      Une thorie scientifique de la culture et autres essais
     </a>
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/radio4/factual/rams/thinkingallowed_20040714.ram">
      Thinking Allowed: Bronislas Malinowski
     </a>
     <br/>
     BBC Radio 4 [28:59]

     [8:21]
     <br/>
     <span style="line-height:17px;font-size:11px;">
      Marcuses lecture at the 1967 London Dialectics of Liberation conference, first 8 minutes, from Peter Villons DVD distributed at the Oct. 2009 Toronto Marcuse conference, which includes discussion with the audience afterward.
     </span>

    <li>
     <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=C5PU0EASi_Q">
      Herbert Marcuse im Gesprch mit Ivo Frenzel und Willy Hochkeppel
     </a>
     [47:02]

    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Ya9KO70FgN8">
      Adorno obit - 1969
     </a>
     [3:39]
     <br/>
     <span style="line-height:17px;font-size:11px;">
      Marcuse thinks that the working class of modern western societies has been integrated into capitalism and does not want to change the running system. According to Marcuse, Adorno saw it the same way. Fighting capitalism has become a matter of personal resistance. Marcuse talks about the merits of Adorno, of how his radical, uncompromising thinking made him immune to corruption by his late fame, of how he represented the best of pre-war European culture.
     </span>
    </li>
   </ul>

     </a>

     </a>

     <span style="line-height:17px;font-size:11px;">
      An independent platform for radical change. Theres a small list of links on Karl Marx, Rosa Luxembourg, Anarchism,  Feminism and liberation movements. Editors: Adriaan Boiten and Noemi Vedi. Dutch and English version.

      Marx and Engels Writings
     </a>
     <br/>
     A collection of writings in economic and social theory, presented by: EServer.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="http://www.cpm.ehime-u.ac.jp/AkamacHomePage/MEMA/MEMA.html">
      Marx-Engels-Marxismus Forschung, Japan
     </a>
     <br/>
     Michio Akama has created a nice index of Japanese contributions to marxist inspired science. Some articles are full text and free, but you wont understand much if you dont speak Japanese.
     <p>

    <li>
     <a href="http://www.anu.edu.au/polsci/marx/marx.html">
      Marxism Page
     </a>
     <br/>
     Contains plain text files of marxist classics, introductions to marxist politics, contemporary marxist material etc. You can even listen to The Internationale if you like (and read the lyrics or background of the song). Created by: Rick Kuhn.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="http://marxistsociology.org/">
      Marxist Sociology Section of the ASA
     </a>
     <br/>
     A resource and meeting point for Marxist scholars from the American Sociological Association. The site provides information on the people of the Marxist Section, Announcements (newsletter, session new), and about Marx and Marxist Theory.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="http://www.marxists.org">
      Marxist Internet Archive
     </a>
     - Colorado
     <br/>
     Contains a library (a chronology of the works of Marx and Engels), a biographical archive, a photo gallery, other marxist writers (like Lenin, Riazanov, Trotsky, and Pannekoek) and a search engine that searches the entire Marx/Engels Internet Library.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="http://www2.iath.virginia.edu/spoons/">
      Spoon Marxism Space, The
     </a>
     (Operations closed, but archive available)
     <br/>
     <span style="line-height:17px;font-size:11px;">
      A marxism space designed to enable diverse yet focussed and experimental discussions on a broad range of issues pertinent to marxism. It is conceived as an environment which increases flexibility, enables more participation, and encourages focus while still promoting cross-fertilization. The site also contains papers in the marxism space archive, archives of discussions and online marxism resources.
     </span>
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     Beamish, Bob [1998] -  (Dept. of Sociology, Queens University, Ontaria, Canada)
     <br/>
     <a href="http://socialistregister.com/index.php/srv/article/view/5708/2604">
      The Making of the Manifesto
     </a>
     <br/>
     In:
     <i>
      Socialist Register
     </i>
     , 34: 218-39.
     <br/>
     <span style="line-height:17px;font-size:11px;">
      A paper presented for the virtual seminar of the Progressive Sociologists Network to celebrate the 150th anniversary of the publication of the Manifesto of the Communist Party. The Manifesto, the most widely read and defining single text in the history of modern socialism, was first published in February, 1848.
     </span>

   </p>
   <ul>
    <img align="right" alt="Maraget Mead" src="../images/sociologists/mead_margaret.jpg"/>
    <span style="line-height:17px;font-size:11px;">
     Never doubt that a small group of thoughtful, committed citizens can change the world, indeed, its the only thing that ever has.
    </span>
    <p>
    </p>
    <li>
     [1949]
     <a href="http://books.google.nl/books/about/Male_and_Female.html?id=fgxhYt9m7ikC&amp;redir_esc=y">
      Male and Female
     </a>
     <br/>
     Mead explains: What is it to be a man? What is it to be a women?
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1962]
     <a href="http://www.worldcat.org/title/online-audio-recordings-margaret-mead-creative-intelligence-female/oclc/40198447">
      Creative Intelligence: Female
     </a>
     <br/>
     Listen to the introduction and questions recorded in 1962 at the Berkeley Language Center (The Silent Revolution: Creative Man in Contemporary Society, 1962)
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="http://www.loc.gov/exhibits/mead/">
      Margaret Mead: Human Nature and the Power of Culture
     </a>
     <br/>
     An online exhibition that commemorates the 100th anniversary of Margaret Meads birth, presented by the Library of Congress (USA). It contains a selection of materials from the extensive Mead collection of the LOC. The collection includes manuscripts, diaries, letters, field notes ,drawings, prints, photographs, sound recordings, and film.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="http://www.amnh.org/exhibitions/permanent-exhibitions/human-origins-and-cultural-halls/margaret-mead-hall-of-pacific-peoples">
      Margaret Mead Hall of Pacific Peoples
     </a>
     <br/>
     Download archival footage of Margeret Mead at the American Museum of Natural History.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="http://anthropology.usf.edu/women/mead/margaret_mead.htm">
      Margeret Mead
     </a>
     <br/>
     A hypertextual biography presented by Celebration of Women Anthropologists.
     <p>

    </li>

      The Women of the Hall: Margaret Mead
     </a>
     <br/>
     A short biography.
     <!--
&lt;P&gt;
&lt;LI&gt;&lt;A HREF="http://casa.colorado.edu/~kachun/mos/ep30.html"&gt;Sex, Lies, and Anthropologists: The Margaret Mead - Derek Freeman Debate&lt;/A&gt; with Dr. Paul Shankman.&lt;br&gt;
In: Research in Anthropology, edited by M. Ember, C. Ember, and D. Levinson. Englewood Cliffs, N.J.: Prentice-Hall.
-->
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="http://freepages.history.rootsweb.ancestry.com/~dav4is/people/STAR1593.htm">
      A list of books by and about Margaret Mead
     </a>
     <br/>
     Presented by Malaspina Great Books Home Page.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     Welty, Gordon [1990]
     <br/>
     <a href="http://www.wright.edu/~gordon.welty/Mead_90.htm">
      The Attack on Mead and the Dialectics of Anthropology
     </a>
     <br/>
     In: Science and Nature 9:14-24.
     <br/>
     A discussion of Derek Freemans 1983 attack on Margaret Meads
     <i>
      Coming of Age in Samoa
     </i>
     (1928). Focus is on the history and significance of the doctrine of Popperian falsifiability in anthropology. Welty argues that the falsifiability canon has a longer history than Popperians acknowledge, dating back at least to Claude Bernards Introduction to the Study of Experimental Medicine [1865]; moreover, this canon entails a dialectical conception of science and its development. In light of these dialectical considerations, it is claimed that Boasian anthropology is the negation of Biologism (sociobiology), and that the dialectical negation of both these doctrines (biologism and Boasian anthropology) is social evolutionism and its philosophical recapitulation, historical materialism.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Margaret_Mead">
      Wikipedia: Margaret _Mead
     </a>
    </li>
   </ul>

    <li>
     Melo, Diane de
     <br/>
     <a href="http://www.umsl.edu/~keelr/200/Diane_Demelo/diane.pdf">
      Mertons Strain Theory
     </a>
     <br/>
     Merton argues that strain is not created by a sudden social change, but rather by a social structure that holds out the same goals to all its members without giving them equal means to achieve them. Mertons theory focusses upon various acts of deviance, which may lead to criminal behavior.  De Melo concentrates her short explanation on the modes of adapting to strain caused by the restricted access to socially approved goals and means.
     <p>
     </p>

      </a>
      <font color="WHITE" size="2">
       <b>
        Pareto, Vilfredo
       </b>
       [1848 - 1923]
      </font>
     </td>
    </tr>
   </table>
   <b>
    Bi(bli)ography
   </b>
   <ul>
    <img align="right" alt="Vilfredo Pareto" hspace="7" src="../images/sociologists/pareto.gif"/>
    <li>
     <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vilfredo_Pareto">
      Wikipedia: Vilfredo_Pareto
     </a>
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="http://www.unil.ch/cwp/">
      Centre detudes interdisciplinaires Walras Pareto
     </a>
     (Universit de Lausanne)
     <br/>
     It includes a biography and bibliography of Pareto. French only.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="http://www.efm.bris.ac.uk/het/pareto/paretobi.htm">
      Selected Primary and Secundary Works
     </a>
     (University of Bristol, UK)
    </li>
   </ul>
   <p>
    <b>
     By Pareto
    </b>
   </p>
   <ul>
    <li>
     [1893]
     <a href="https://archive.org/stream/parliamentaryrg00paregoog#page/n103/mode/2up">
      The Parliamentary Rgime in Italy
     </a>
     <br/>
     In:
     <i>
      Political Science Quarterly
     </i>
     , 8:677-721
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1893]
     <a href="http://www.unil.ch/cwp/docs/Pman.html">
      Leon dconomie pure  lUniversit de Lausanne
     </a>
     [Moved to ?]
     <br/>
     In:
     <i>
      History of Economics Ideas,
     </i>
     5(3), 1997.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1897]
     <a href="http://socserv2.socsci.mcmaster.ca/~econ/ugcm/3ll3/pareto/theories">
      The New Theories of Economics
     </a>
     <br/>
     <i>
      In:
      <i>
       Journal of Political Economy
      </i>
      ,
     </i>
     5
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1916]
     <a href="https://archive.org/stream/trattatodisocio00paregoog#page/n1/mode/2up">
      Trattato di sociologia generale
     </a>
     |
     <a href="http://www.marxists.org/reference/subject/philosophy/works/it/pareto.htm">
      Mind &amp; Society
     </a>
     <br/>
     This is considered Paretos greatest work, in which he inquires into the nature and bases of individual and social action. He argues that social classes are formed because persons of superior ability seek to confirm and aggrandise their social position. In an effort to rise into the elite of the upper strata, privileged members of the lower-class groups continually strive to use their abilities and thus improve them; the opposite tendency obtains among the elite. The best-equipped persons from the lower class rise to challenge the position of the upper-class elite. This is the famous circulation of elites.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1919]
     <a href="https://archive.org/stream/manualedieconomi00pareuoft#page/n5/mode/2up">
      Manuale di Economia Politica con una Introduzione alla Scienza Sociale
     </a>
     <br/>
     Milano: Societa Edtrice Libraria
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1920]
     <a href="https://archive.org/stream/compendiodesocio00pareuoft#page/n5/mode/2up">
      Compendio di Sociologia Generale
     </a>
     <br/>
     Firenze: Barbra
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1935]
     <a href="http://media.pfeiffer.edu/lridener/courses/CIRCELIT.HTML">
      Circulation of the Elites
     </a>
     <br/>
     From Vilfredo Pareto [1935]
     <i>
      The Mind and Society,
     </i>
     ed. Arthur Livingston trans. Andrew Bongiomo (NewYork: Harcourt, Brace &amp; Co.), Vols. III and IV, Sections 2026-9 and Sections 2233-6.
    </li>
   </ul>
   <b>
    On Pareto
   </b>
   <ul>
    <li>
     Bruni, Luigino / Montesano, Aldo [2009]
     <br/>
     <a href="https://books.google.nl/books?id=hqR8AgAAQBAJ">
      New Essays on Pareto's Economic Theory
     </a>
     <br/>
     Routledge
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     Thornton, Fr. James [1997]
     <br/>
     <a href="http://jkalb.freeshell.org/misc/pareto.html">
      Vilfredo Pareto: A Concise Overview of His Life, Works, and Philosophy
     </a>
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     Zanni, Alberto [1999]
     <br/>
     <a href="http://www.dse.unifi.it/spe/indici/numero38/zanni.htm">
      Pareto in Toscana: le discontinuit e i prodromi di un economista sociologo
     </a>
     (Italian)
     <br/>
     In: Storia del pensiero economico, 38: 3-35
    </li>
   </ul>

    <a name="POPPER">

   <table cellpadding="4" width="100%">
    <tr>
     <td bgcolor="#336699">
      <a href="#top" target="_self">
       <img align="right" alt="Index" border="0" src="../images/up.gif"/>
      </a>
      <font color="WHITE" size="2">
       <b>
        Popper, Karl Reimund
       </b>
       [1902 - 1994]
      </font>
     </td>
    </tr>
   </table>
   <p>
    <b>
     <i>
      By Popper
     </i>
    </b>
   </p>
   <ul>
    <img align="right" alt="Karl Popper" src="../images/sociologists/popper.jpg"/>
    <li>
     [1934/1959]
     <a href="https://archive.org/stream/PopperLogicScientificDiscovery/popper-logic-scientific-discovery#page/n3/mode/2up">
      The Logic of Scientific Discovery
     </a>
     <br/>
     London/New York: Routledge
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1972]
     <a href="http://cla.calpoly.edu/~fotoole/321.1/popper.html">
      Science: Conjectures and Refutations
     </a>
     <br/>
     <span style="line-height:17px;font-size:11px;">
      Popper explains the apparent progress of scientific knowledgehow it is that our understanding of the universe seems to improve over time. This problem arises from his position that the truth content of our theories, even the best of them, cannot be verified by scientific testing, but can only be falsified. If so, then how is it that the growth of science appears to result in a growth in knowledge?
     </span>
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1994]
     <a href="http://old.lf3.cuni.cz/aff/p2_e.html">
      Prague Lecture
     </a>
    </li>
   </ul>
   <p>
    <b>
     <i>
      On Popper
     </i>
    </b>
   </p>
   <ul>
    <li>
     Burgess, Mike [1996]
     <br/>
     <a href="http://www.tkpw.net/cafe/etc/burgess95.txt">
      A discussion of Karl Poppers critique of  Marxism in
      <i>
       The Open Society and its Enemies, and The Poverty of Historicism
      </i>
     </a>
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     Gardner, Martin [2001]
     <br/>
     <a href="http://www.stephenjaygould.org/ctrl/gardner_popper.html">
      A Skeptical Look at Karl Popper
     </a>
     <br/>
     In:
     <a href="http://www.csicop.org/si/">
      Skeptical Inquirer
     </a>
     , 25(4): 13-4,72.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     Jira, Milan [1994]
     <br/>
     <a href="http://old.lf3.cuni.cz/aff/popper_e.html">
      Sir Karl Popper in Prague, May 23-27, 1994
     </a>
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     Hickey, Thomas J. [1995/2005]
     <br/>
     <a href="http://www.philsci.com/book5.htm">
      Karl Popper and fasificationist criticism
     </a>
     <br/>
     In: idem, History of Twentieth-Century Philosophy of Science, Book V.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     Singer, Peter [1974]
     <br/>
     <a href="http://www.utilitarianism.net/singer/by/19740502.htm">
      Discovering Karl Popper
     </a>
     <br/>
     In:
     <i>
      The New York Review of Books
     </i>
     , 21(2) (May 2, 1974].

    <li>

     [1776/1778]
     <a href="http://abu.cnam.fr/cgi-bin/go?reveries3">
      Les rveries du promeneur solitaire
     </a>
     (Abu) |
     <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0199563276/ref=as_li_tf_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=9325&amp;creativeASIN=0199563276&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=sociosite-20">
      Reveries of the Solitary Walker
     </a>
     <img alt="" border="0" height="1" src="http://ir-na.amazon-adsystem.com/e/ir?t=sociosite-20&amp;l=as2&amp;o=1&amp;a=0199563276" style="border:none !important; margin:0px !important;" width="1"/>
     (Amazon)
     <br/>
     Rousseaus last great work is part reminiscence, part meditation, as the philosopher tries to come to terms with his isolation and to find happiness in solitude and nature. The Reveries are an important complement to Rousseaus other works and address many of the same issues. Its a useful introduction for anyone interested in reading Rousseau for the first time. The English translation of Russell Goulbourne offers a fresh new translation that marries accuracy with readability. The book features detailed explanatory notes that enable readers to appreciate to the full Rousseau's ideas, ranging from biographical details to literary allusions, philosophical contexts, and the routes around Paris where Rousseau walked.
     <p>
     </p>

    <p>
     <img align="right" alt="Frederick Winslow Taylor" src="../images/sociologists/taylor.jpg"/>

    <li>
     <a href="https://www.stevens.edu/library/collections/frederick-winslow-taylor">
      F. W. Taylor Collection
     </a>
     <br/>
     The F. W. Taylor Project is preserving and disseminating the F. W. Taylor Collection at the Stevens Institute of Technology by establishing the on-line Taylor archive to digitally store and represent the contents of the collection. The Taylor archive is described in the
     <i>
      Classified Guide to the Frederick Winslow Tayler Collection
     </i>
     . Editor: Doris Oliver.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1911]
     <a href="https://archive.org/stream/principlesofscie00tayl#page/n5/mode/2up">
      The Principles of Scientific Management
     </a>
     [Archive.org] |
     <a href="http://socserv.mcmaster.ca/econ/ugcm/3ll3/taylor/sciman">
      idem
     </a>
     [Text provided by Eric Eldred]
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1911/1919]
     <a href="https://archive.org/stream/shopmanagement00tayl#page/n7/mode/2up">
      Shop Management
     </a>
     <br/>
     New York/London: Harper &amp; Brothers
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1912]
     <a href="https://archive.org/stream/charterhouseoflo00tayluoft#page/n9/mode/2up">
      The Charterhoud of London
     </a>
     <br/>
     New York: Dutton
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="http://gilbrethnetwork.tripod.com">
      Frank and Lillian Gilbreth
     </a>
     <br/>
     The Gilbreths motion studies on how a task was done, and how best to eliminate unneeded, fatiguing steps in any process. Their work is commonly linked with Taylors time studies and grouped within the various laws and principles of scientific management. See also the illustration of Gilbreths motion studies in domestic spaces:
     <a href="http://americanhistory.si.edu/ontime/saving/kitchen.html">
      Dr. Gilbreth's Kitchen
     </a>
     .
    </li>
   </ul>

      On Taylor

    <li>
     Becker, T. [1996]
     <br/>
     <a href="http://paedagogik.homepage.t-online.de/indu_wa.htm">
      Industrieller und technologischer Wandel
     </a>
     <br/>
     An analysis of the history of production methods: pre-industrial production, industrial mass production (Taylorism, Fordism) en Toyotisms.

      Von Taylor und Ford zur lean production
     </a>
     <br/>
     Analyses the historical development of mass production, the introduction of taylorism in Europe, and emergence of the flexible or lean production in Japan.

   </ul>

   <p>
    <b>
     <i>

   <ul>
    <img align="right" alt="Alexis de Tocqueville" src="../images/sociologists/tocqueville.jpg"/>
    <li>
     [1835]
     <a href="http://xroads.virginia.edu/~HYPER/DETOC/home.html">
      Democracy in America
     </a>
     <br/>
     Still one of the most influential works in political thought. Tocquevilles America is a project of the American Studies Programs at The University of Virginia. They take up the task of re-contextualizing Tocquevilles famous political and cultural analysis of American democracy. The objective is, over time, to return that book to its origins, to the America of 1831-32. For it was on that very specific ground and at that very specific historical moment that Tocqueville stood.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1837]

    <a name="TONNIES">
    </a>
   </p>
   <table cellpadding="4" width="100%">
    <tr>
     <td bgcolor="#336699">
      <a href="#top" target="_self">
       <img align="right" alt="Index" border="0" src="../images/up.gif"/>
      </a>
      <font color="WHITE" size="2">
       <b>
        Tnnies, Ferdinand
       </b>
       [1855 - 1936]
      </font>
     </td>
    </tr>
   </table>
   <ul>
    <img align="right" alt="Ferdinand Tnnies" src="../images/sociologists/toennies.gif"/>
    <li>
     <a href="http://www.ftg-kiel.de">
      Ferdinand Tnnies-Gesellschaft
     </a>
     <br/>
     The aim of the Ferdinand Tnnies Society is to cultivate the spiritual legacy of Tnnies. The FTG maintains a Tnnies-Forum (free for members). The main activitie is the realisation of the complete works of Tnnies (De Gruyter).
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1887]
     <a href="http://media.pfeiffer.edu/lridener/courses/GEMEIN.HTML">
      On Gemeinschaft
and Gesellschaft
     </a>
     <br/>
     Reprinted from
     <i>
      Community and Society: Gemeinschaft und Gesellschaft
     </i>
     by Ferdinand Tonnies, translated and edited by Charles P. Loomis, pp. 223-31. 1957, The Michigan State University Press.
     <br/>
     Tonnies makes a distinction between two basic types of social groups. Groups in which the membership is based on a feeling of togetherness he termed
     <i>
      Gemeinschaft
     </i>
     (often translated as community). Groups in which membership is sustained by some instrumental goal or definite endhe termed
     <i>
      Gesellschaft
     </i>
     (often translated as society). Gemeinschaft is exemplified by the family or neighborhood; Gesellschaft, by the city or the state.
     <br/>
     See also the German original
     <a href="http://www.deutschestextarchiv.de/book/show/toennies_gemeinschaft_1887">
      Gemeinschaft und Gesellschat. Abhandlung des Communismus und des Sozioalismus als empirischer Culturformen
     </a>
     and the explication of
     <a href="http://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gemeinschaft_und_Gesellschaft">
      Gemeinschaft und Gesellschaft
     </a>
     .
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1896]
     <a href="https://archive.org/stream/hobbeslebenundl00tngoog#page/n9/mode/2up">
      Hobbes Leben und Lehre
     </a>
     <br/>
     Stuttgart: Fromanns Verlag
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1897]
     <a href="https://archive.org/stream/ueberdiegrundth00tngoog#page/n5/mode/2up">
      ber die Grondtatsachen des sozialen Lebens
     </a>
     <br/>
     Bern: Von Steiger
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1906]
     <a href="https://archive.org/stream/philosophischete00tn#page/n3/mode/2up">
      Philosophische Terminologie in psychologisch-soziologischer Ansicht
     </a>
     <br/>
     Leipzig: Verlang von Theod. Thomas
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1915]
     <a href="https://archive.org/stream/warlikeenglandas00tn#page/n3/mode/2up">
      Warlike England - A Seen by Herself
     </a>
     <br/>
     New York: Dillingham
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1919]
     <a href="https://archive.org/stream/entwicklungderso00tonn#page/n3/mode/2up">
      Die Entwicklung der sozialen  Frage bis zum Weltkriege
     </a>
     <br/>
     Berlin/Leipzig: Walter de Gruyter
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1922]

     <br/>
     Berlin: Julius Springer
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="http://www.ftg-kiel.de/ftg.htm">

     </a>
     <br/>
     Complete works of Tnnies by De Gruyter.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     Deflem, Mathieu [1999] (Purdue University)
     <br/>
     <a href="http://deflem.blogspot.com/1999/08/ferdinand-tonnies-on-crime-and-society.html">
      Ferdinand Tnnies on Crime and Society - An Unexplored Contribution to Criminological Sociology
     </a>
     [
     <a href="https://docs.google.com/file/d/0BwJtnhSgn6Ozd0Y5RDBQb210bW8/edit">
      pdf
     </a>
     ]
     <br/>
     In:
     <i>
      History of the Human Sciences
     </i>
     12(3): 87-116.
     <p>

   <a name="TOYNBEE">
   </a>
   <table cellpadding="4" width="100%">
    <tr>
     <td bgcolor="#336699">
      <a href="#top" target="_self">
       <img align="right" alt="Index" border="0" src="../images/up.gif"/>
      </a>
      <font color="WHITE" size="2">
       <b>
        Toynbee, Arnold
       </b>
       [1852 - 1883]
      </font>
     </td>
    </tr>
   </table>
   <ul>
    <img align="right" alt="Arnold Toynbee" src="../images/sociologists/toynbee.gif"/>
    <p>
    </p>
    <li>
     <a href="http://www.toynbeehall.org.uk">
      Toynbee Hall
     </a>
     <br/>
     The official Toynbee site.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arnold_Toynbee">
      Wikipedia: Arnold_Toynbee
     </a>
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     [1884]
     <a href="http://www.efm.bris.ac.uk/het/toynbee/indrev">
      Lectures on The Industrial Revolution in England
     </a>
     |
     <a href="http://www.efm.bris.ac.uk/het/toynbee/indrev">
      mirror
     </a>
     <br/>
     Discusses the industrial and agrarian revolution at the end of the 18th and beginning of the 19th centuries. The first part deals with Adam Smith (England on the eve of the Industrial revolution and the causes of wealth), the second part deals with Malthus (distribution of wealth and causes of poverty), the third part deals with Ricardo (doctrine of rent and wages and theories of economic progress).
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="http://records.viu.ca/~mcneil/cit/citlctoyn.htm">
      Library of Congress Citations
     </a>
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     Marshall, Alfred [1887]
     <br/>
     <a href="http://www.disei.unifi.it/upload/sub/pubblicazioni/msb/1996/toynbee6.pdf">
      On Arnold Toynbee
     </a>
     <br/>
     From: A. Marshall
     <i>
      On Arnold Toynbee
     </i>
     , introduced and edited by John K. Wothaker,
     <i>
      Marshall Studies Bulletin
     </i>
     8: 45-8.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="http://creativequotations.com/one/1426.htm">
      Creative Quotations from Arnold Toynbee (1852-1883)
     </a>
     <br/>
     For instance: It is a paradoxical but profound true and important principle of life that the most likely way to reach a goal is to be aiming not at that goal itself but at some more ambitious goal beyond it.
    </li>
   </ul>

   </p>
   <ul>
    <li>
     Halas, Elzbieta [2001]
     <br/>
     <a href="http://www.lrz-muenchen.de/~Prof.Helle/znaniecki1.htm">
      The Humanistic Approach of Florian Znaniecki
     </a>
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     Halas, Elzbieta [2006]
     <br/>
     <a href="http://jcs.sagepub.com/cgi/reprint/6/3/257.pdf">
      Classical Cultural Sociology: Florian Znanieckis Impact in a New Light
     </a>
     <br/>
     In:
     <i>
      Journal of Classical Sociology
     </i>
     . 6:257-282.
    </li>
   </ul>
   <p clear="all">
    <a name="REF">
    </a>
   </p>
   <table cellpadding="4" width="100%">
    <tr>
     <th bgcolor="#336699">
      <a href="#top" target="_self">
       <img align="right" alt="Index" border="0" src="../images/up.gif"/>
      </a>
      <font color="WHITE" size="3">
       References
      </font>
     </th>
    </tr>
   </table>
   <ul>
    <li>
     <a href="http://classiques.uqac.ca">
      Les Classiques des sciences sociales
     </a>
     +
     <a href="http://classiques.uqac.ca/contemporains/">
      Les sciences sociales contemporaines
     </a>
     (Universit du Qubec  Chicoutimi)
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="http://media.pfeiffer.edu/lridener/DSS/DEADSOC.HTML">
      Dead Sociologists Society
     </a>
     <br/>
     A list of the various theorists, some biographical information and a summary of their work. Comte, Marx, Spencer, Durkheim, Simmel, Weber, Veblen, Cooley, Mead, Park, Pareto and Sorokin.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="http://www.ethologic.com/sasha/links/thinkers.html">
      Great Thinkers and Visionaries
     </a>
     <br/>
     The live and works of great thinkers, from Leonado Da Vinci via  Newton and Einstein to  Chomsky and Hawking. Provided by Alexander Chislenko.
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="homepages.php">
      Personal Home pages of Sociologists
      <sub>
       <img border="0" src="../images/next.gif"/>
      </sub>
     </a>
     (SocioSite)
     <p>
     </p>
    </li>
    <li>
     <a href="http://www.studymore.org.uk/sshtim.htm">
      Time line for the history of sciene and social science
     </a>
     <br/>
     A time line from before writing began to the present, linked to Andrew Roberts book
     <i>
      Social Science History
     </i>
     and to other resources, including extracts and works of authors. The alphabetical index of authors is very helpful. And so is the
     <a href="http://www.studymore.org.uk/glossary.htm">
      ABC Study Guide
     </a>
     in plain English.
    </li>
   </ul>
